These alignments together with an unrooted phylogenetic tree (constructed as described above) were used for subsequent molecular evolutionary analysis. For the estimation of the lineage-specific evolutionary rate, the values of <i>K</i><sub>a</sub>, <i>K</i><sub>s</sub> and <i>K</i><sub>a</sub>/<i>K</i><sub>s</sub> were calculated for 10,000 concatenated alignments constructed from 150 randomly chosen genes using the Codeml programme with the free-ratio model in the Phylogenetic Analysis by Maximum Likelihood<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 53" title="Yang, Z. PAML 4: phylogenetic analysis by maximum likelihood. Mol. Biol. Evol. 24, 1586â1591 (2007)." href="/articles/ncomms3797#ref-CR53" id="ref-link-section-d37838e2577">53</a></sup> package. To detect PSGs in either <i>P. euphratica</i> or <i>P. trichocarpa</i> lineage, the lineage was specified in turn as the foreground branch. We then used the optimized branch-site model<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 55" title="Zhang, J., Nielsen, R. &amp; Yang, Z. Evaluation of an improved branch-site likelihood method for detecting positive selection at the molecular Level. Mol. Biol. Evol. 22, 2472â2479 (2005)." href="/articles/ncomms3797#ref-CR55" id="ref-link-section-d37838e2587">55</a></sup> in which likelihood ratio test <i>P-</i>values were computed, assuming that the null distribution was a 50:50 mixture of a <i>Ï</i><sup>2</sup>-distribution with one degree of freedom and a point mass at zero. To minimize the false discovery rate, we manually filtered all PSGs with potential errors in their alignments.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec14">Transcriptome sequencing and analysis</h3><p>Total RNAs were extracted and strand-specific RNA-seq libraries were generated from samples using a cetyl trimethylammonium bromide procedure<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 56" title="Chang, S., Puryear, J. &amp; Cairney, J. A simple and efficient method for isolating RNA from pine trees. Plant Mol. Biol. Rep. 11, 113â116 (1993)." href="/articles/ncomms3797#ref-CR56" id="ref-link-section-d37838e2607">56</a></sup> for transcriptome sequencing. The analysis was conducted on pooled samples of roots, leaves, flower buds, flowers, xylem and phloem from two mature male <i>P. euphratica</i> trees and one mature female tree from the Talim Basin desert, Xinjiang, on control samples and also on salt-stressed samples (200âmM NaCl for 6, 12, 24 and 48âh) generated from the same calluses used in genome sequencing. RNA-seq libraries were sequenced on an Illumina Genome Analyzer platform. In addition, salt-stressed leaves and roots were collected and RNA samples were isolated for Illumina short-read sequencing. Three independent biological replicate samples were examined. The resulting reads were aligned to the <i>P. euphratica</i> genome sequences using TopHat<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 48" title="Trapnell, C., Pachter, L. &amp; Salzberg, S. L. TopHat: discovering splice junctions with RNA-Seq. Bioinformatics 25, 1105â1111 (2009)." href="/articles/ncomms3797#ref-CR48" id="ref-link-section-d37838e2617">48</a></sup>. After alignment, the count of mapped reads from each sample was derived and normalized to fragments per kilobase of exon per million fragments mapped for each predicted transcript using the Cufflinks<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 49" title="Trapnell, C. et al. Transcript assembly and quantification by RNA-Seq reveals unannotated transcripts and isoform switching during cell differentiation. Nat. Biotechnol. 28, 511â515 (2010)." href="/articles/ncomms3797#ref-CR49" id="ref-link-section-d37838e2621">49</a></sup> package. DEGs were identified using the programme Cuffdiff in the Cufflinks package. We had tried to induce the calluses from <i>P. trichocarpa</i>, but they grew too slowly. We therefore sequenced transcriptomes of <i>P. tomentosa</i> calluses that had been subjected to salt-stress treatment (200âmM NaCl for 0, 6, 12, 24 and 48âh) and identified DEGs in this salt-sensitive species. In addition to the analysis as described for <i>P. euphratica</i>, we further assembled and annotated all reads from <i>P. tomentosa</i> using Trinity<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 57" title="Grabherr, M. G. et al. Full-length transcriptome assembly from RNA-Seq data without a reference genome. Nat. Biotechnol. 29, 644â652 (2011)." href="/articles/ncomms3797#ref-CR57" id="ref-link-section-d37838e2638">57</a></sup> package (<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/ncomms3797#MOESM760">Supplementary Methods</a>). We used the InParanoid<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 58" title="Berglund, A. C., Sjolund, E., Ostlund, G. &amp; Sonnhammer, E. L. InParanoid 6: eukaryotic ortholog clusters with inparalogs. Nucleic Acids Res. 36, D263âD266 (2008)." href="/articles/ncomms3797#ref-CR58" id="ref-link-section-d37838e2646">58</a></sup> software to identify 1:1 orthologues between <i>P. euphratica</i> and <i>P. tomentosa</i>, and aligned the coding sequences of the orthologues using Threaded Blockset Aligner<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 59" title="Blanchette, M. et al. Aligning multiple genomic sequences with the threaded blockset aligner. Genome Res. 14, 708â715 (2004)." href="/articles/ncomms3797#ref-CR59" id="ref-link-section-d37838e2656">59</a></sup> to extract perfectly aligned consensus blocks. Finally, we counted the reads aligned to the consensus blocks for each sample and performed edgeR<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 60" title="Robinson, M. D., McCarthy, D. J. &amp; Smyth, G. K. edgeR: a Bioconductor package for differential expression analysis of digital gene expression data. Bioinformatics 26, 139â140 (2010)." href="/articles/ncomms3797#ref-CR60" id="ref-link-section-d37838e2660">60</a></sup> in R package to identify DEGs.</p></div></div></section><section aria-labelledby="Sec15" data-title="Additional information"><div class="c-article-section" id="Sec15-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="Sec15">Additional information</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="Sec15-content"><p><b>Accession codes</b>: The whole-genome shotgun project has been deposited in DDBJ/EMBL/GenBank nucleotide core database under the accession code <a href="http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/nuccore/?term=AOFL00000000">AOFL00000000</a>. The version described in this paper is the first version, <a href="http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/nuccore/?term=AOFL01000000">AOFL01000000</a>. All short-read data have been deposited in the Sequence Read Archive (SRA) under accession <a href="http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/sra?term=SRA061340">SRA061340</a>. Raw sequence data of the transcriptomes have been deposited in the SRA under accession codes <a href="http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/sra?term=SRP028829">SRP028829</a> and <a href="http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/sra?term=SRP028830">SRP028830</a>.</p><p><b>How to cite this article:</b> Ma, T. <i>et al.</i> Genomic insights into salt adaptation in a desert poplar. <i>Nat. Commun.</i> 4:2797 doi: 10.1038/ncomms3797 (2013).</p></div></div></section>

Jun Wang led the genome sequencing. Juan Wang and Q.W. prepared the <i>P. euphratica</i> nucleic acid samples. Junyi Wang, Z.Y., G.Z., D.J., S.P., D.F., Yadan Luo, X.L. and H.Y. performed the DNA sequencing. Z.Y., Y.C., Z.W., C.G., L.Y., D.Z. and Jinchao Liu performed the genome assembly. Junyi Wang, Y.C., Z.W., X.W., G.W., Z.C., Yao Lu and Ye Yin performed the genome annotation. T.M., Q.H. and Q.Q. designed evolutionary analyses. T.M., G.Z., Y.C., J.Z., Q.Q., K.W., D.J., R.Z. and W.L. performed evolutionary analyses. Q.H., T.M., J.Z., K.W. and W.L. performed the synteny analyses. K.W., T.M., B.L. and H.M. performed the transcriptome analyses. Q.H., B.L. and Yongzhi Yang carried out data submission and database construction. T.M. and Jianquan Liu wrote the paper. G.A.T., S.P.D., R.J.A., Jun Wang, M.L., T.Y., Jia Li, D.W. and Y.W. revised the paper.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="corresponding-author">Corresponding authors</h3><p id="corresponding-author-list">Correspondence to
